</P></TD></TR></TABLE>

<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Cash provided by operating activities was $3.9&nbsp;billion; Free Cash Flow<SUP
STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">1</SUP> was $2.9&nbsp;billion </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Return of capital to shareholders was $3.4&nbsp;billion </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">DEERFIELD, Ill. &#150; January&nbsp;30, 2019 &#150; Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (NASDAQ: MDLZ) today reported its fourth quarter and
full-year 2018 results. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">&#147;Our fourth quarter and full-year 2018 results demonstrate the power of our brands, the strength of our
global footprint and the potential of our strategic plan,&#148; said Dirk Van de Put, Chairman and CEO. &#147;We delivered on our key financial and strategic commitments for the year, including solid <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">top-line</FONT>
and bottom-line growth and strong cash flow generation. In 2019, we will continue to progress against our new strategy, which includes new investments to drive organic revenue growth and operational excellence across the organization.&#148; </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><U>Key Strategic Initiatives </U></I></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Launched a new approach to marketing including more balanced investment across both global and iconic local
brands to fully leverage the company&#146;s portfolio and category-leading positions </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Developed a more locally-oriented commercial structure to drive greater consumer focus, improve speed and reduce
complexity </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Introduced new incentive structure effective in 2019 to drive better alignment with key financial metrics to
reward entrepreneurial behavior and quality of results </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Initiated expansion of research, development and quality capabilities to drive innovation, including a new
technical center in India and additional investment in a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">state-of-the-art</FONT></FONT></FONT> facility in Poland </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Deployed &#145;test, learn and scale&#146; approach to innovation and launched SnackFutures, an innovation hub
focused on the invention and reinvention of new brands, and venturing with entrepreneurs to seed new businesses in key strategic areas </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="5%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt">Announced divestiture of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-core</FONT> cheese business in the Middle
East&nbsp;&amp; Africa, increasing the company&#146;s focus on snacking </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

STYLE="white-space:nowrap">zero-net</FONT> waste packaging and expanded the Cocoa Life sustainability program in Brazil </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Net Revenue

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><U>Fourth Quarter Commentary </U></I></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Net revenues</B> declined 2.8&nbsp;percent, driven by the impact of currency. Organic Net Revenue increased
2.5&nbsp;percent driven by continued strength in emerging markets with a good balance of volume/mix and pricing. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Gross profit</B> declined $104&nbsp;million and margin decreased 50 basis points to 37.6&nbsp;percent, driven
primarily by higher restructuring costs. Adjusted Gross Profit increased $147&nbsp;million at constant currency and margin increased 90 basis points to 40.0&nbsp;percent, driven by higher pricing and productivity savings partially offset by higher
raw material costs. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Operating income </B>grew $40&nbsp;million and margin increased 90 basis points to 12.8&nbsp;percent,
primarily due to the lapping of prior-year malware-related expenses and the benefit of an indirect tax matter. Adjusted Operating Income increased $79&nbsp;million at constant currency and margin increased 50 basis points to 16.2&nbsp;percent due to
pricing and productivity savings partially offset by higher raw material costs and increased selling, general and administrative expenses. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Diluted EPS</B> was $0.56, up 22&nbsp;percent driven primarily by Adjusted EPS growth. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Adjusted EPS</B> was $0.63, up 21&nbsp;percent on a constant-currency basis, driven primarily by increased
equity income and operating gains. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

approximately $400&nbsp;million in cash dividends. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><U>Full Year Commentary </U></I></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Net revenues</B> increased 0.2&nbsp;percent, despite the impact of currency and divestitures. Organic Net
Revenue increased 2.4&nbsp;percent. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Gross profit was</B> up $318&nbsp;million and margin increased 120 basis points to 39.9&nbsp;percent. This
change was driven primarily by favorable <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> gains from currency and commodity hedging activities and lapping prior-year incremental malware costs. Adjusted
Gross Profit dollars increased $352&nbsp;million at constant currency and margin increased 40 basis points to 40.1&nbsp;percent. This increase was driven primarily by higher pricing and productivity savings, partially offset by higher raw material
costs. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Operating income </B>decreased $150&nbsp;million and margin decreased<B> </B>60 basis points to
12.8&nbsp;percent, driven primarily by the impact from pension participation changes in North America and lapping the prior-year gain on a divestiture and prior-year benefit of an indirect tax matter. These unfavorable items were partially offset by
favorable change in <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> gains from currency and commodity hedging activities, lower restructuring program costs and the lapping of prior-year malware-related
expenses. Adjusted Operating Income increased $257&nbsp;million at constant currency and margin increased 60 basis points to 16.7&nbsp;percent due primarily to Adjusted Gross Margin expansion. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Diluted EPS </B>was $2.28, up 23&nbsp;percent driven primarily by an
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax</FONT> gain on the Keurig Dr Pepper transaction, favorable <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> gains from currency and commodity hedging activities
and lower restructuring program costs partially offset by the impact from pension participation changes. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR style = "page-break-inside:avoid">
<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">&#149;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Adjusted EPS</B> was $2.43 and grew 15&nbsp;percent on a constant-currency basis, driven primarily by
operating gains, share repurchases, increased equity income and tax favorability. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>

<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Cash provided by operating activities </B>was $3.9&nbsp;billion. Free Cash Flow was $2.9&nbsp;billion. Cash
flow was primarily driven by working capital improvements and improved cash earnings. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="1%">&nbsp;</TD>

<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>Capital Return</B>: The company returned $3.4&nbsp;billion of capital to shareholders through $2&nbsp;billion
in share repurchases and $1.4&nbsp;billion in dividends. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>2019 Outlook </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International provides guidance on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> basis, as the company cannot predict some
elements that are included in reported GAAP results, including the impact of foreign exchange. Refer to the Outlook section in the discussion of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures below for more details. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company continues to expect Organic Net Revenue growth to be between 2 and 3&nbsp;percent. The company maintains its outlook for Adjusted
EPS growth of 3 to 5&nbsp;percent on a constant-currency basis. The company estimates currency translation would decrease net revenue growth by approximately 3 percent<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">3</SUP> with a negative $0.07
impact to Adjusted EPS<SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">3</SUP>. In addition, the company continues to expect Free Cash Flow of approximately $2.8&nbsp;billion. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Conference Call </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International will host a conference call for investors with accompanying slides to review its results at 5 p.m. ET today. A
listen-only webcast will be provided at <U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U>. An archive of the webcast will be available on the company&#146;s web site. The company will be live tweeting the event at <U>www.twitter.com/MDLZ</U>. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>About Mondel&#275;z International </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (NASDAQ: MDLZ) empowers people to snack right in over 150 countries around the world. With 2018 net revenues
of approximately $26&nbsp;billion, MDLZ is leading the future of snacking with iconic global and local brands such as <I>Oreo</I>, <I>belVita</I> and <I>LU</I> biscuits; <I>Cadbury Dairy Milk</I>, <I>Milka</I> and <I>Toblerone</I> chocolate; <I>Sour
Patch Kids</I> candy and <I>Trident</I> gum. Mondel&#275;z International is a proud member of the Standard and Poor&#146;s 500, Nasdaq 100 and Dow Jones Sustainability Index. Visit <U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U> or follow the company on
Twitter at <U>www.twitter.com/MDLZ</U>. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>End Notes </B></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD WIDTH="4%">&nbsp;</TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left">1.</TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">Organic Net Revenue, Adjusted Gross Profit (and Adjusted Gross Profit margin), Adjusted Operating Income (and
Adjusted Operating Income margin), Adjusted EPS, Free Cash Flow and presentation of amounts in constant currency are <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures. Please see discussion of
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures at the end of this press release for more information. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>

<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Additional Definitions </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Emerging markets
consist of the Latin America region in its entirety; the Asia, Middle East and Africa region excluding Australia, New Zealand and Japan; and the following countries from the Europe region: Russia, Ukraine, Turkey, Kazakhstan, Belarus, Georgia,
Poland, Czech Republic, Slovak Republic, Hungary, Bulgaria, Romania, the Baltics and the East Adriatic countries. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Developed markets
include the entire North America region, the Europe region excluding the countries included in the emerging markets definition, and Australia, New Zealand and Japan from the Asia, Middle East and Africa region. </P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Forward-Looking Statements </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">This press release contains a number of forward-looking statements. Words, and variations of words, such as &#147;will,&#148;
&#147;expect,&#148; &#147;may,&#148; &#147;would,&#148; &#147;could,&#148; &#147;deliver,&#148; &#147;potential,&#148; &#147;estimate,&#148; &#147;guidance,&#148; &#147;outlook&#148; and similar expressions are intended to identify the
company&#146;s forward-looking statements, including, but not limited to, statements about: the company&#146;s future performance, including its future revenue growth, earnings per share and cash flow; currency and the effect of foreign exchange
translation on the company&#146;s results of operations; the impact of U.S. tax reform; the company&#146;s liability related to withdrawal from the Bakery and Confectionery Union and Industry International Pension Fund; the Brazilian indirect tax
matter; the impacts of the malware incident; strategic transactions; the company&#146;s strategy and investments; and the company&#146;s outlook, including 2019 Organic Net Revenue growth, Adjusted EPS and Free Cash Flow. These forward-looking
statements are subject to a number of risks and uncertainties, many of which are beyond the company&#146;s control, which could cause the company&#146;s actual results to differ materially from those indicated in the company&#146;s forward-looking
statements. Such factors include, but are not limited to, risks from operating globally including in emerging markets; changes in currency exchange rates, controls and restrictions; continued volatility of commodity and other input costs; weakness
in economic conditions; weakness in consumer spending; pricing actions; tax matters including changes in tax rates and laws, disagreements with taxing authorities and imposition of new taxes; use of information technology and third party service
providers; unanticipated disruptions to the company&#146;s business, such as the malware incident, cyberattacks or other security breaches; competition; the restructuring program and the company&#146;s other transformation initiatives not yielding
the anticipated benefits; and changes in the assumptions on which the restructuring program is based. Please also see the company&#146;s risk factors, as they may be amended from time to time, set forth in its filings with the SEC, including the
company&#146;s most recently filed Annual Report on Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">10-K.</FONT> Mondelez International disclaims and does not undertake any obligation to update or revise any forward-looking statement in this press release,
except as required by applicable law or regulation. </P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:14pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. and Subsidiaries </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:12pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>Reconciliation of GAAP and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> Financial Measures </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:12pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>(Unaudited) </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company reports its
financial results in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted in the United States (&#147;GAAP&#148;). However, management believes that also presenting certain <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures
provides additional information to facilitate comparison of the company&#146;s historical operating results and trends in its underlying operating results, and provides additional transparency on how the company evaluates its business. Management
uses these <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures in making financial, operating and planning decisions and in evaluating the company&#146;s performance. The company also believes that presenting these measures allows
investors to view its performance using the same measures that the company uses in evaluating its financial and business performance and trends. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
company considers quantitative and qualitative factors in assessing whether to adjust for the impact of items that may be significant or that could affect an understanding of its ongoing financial and business performance and trends. The adjustments
generally fall within the following categories: acquisition&nbsp;&amp; divestiture activities, gains and losses on intangible asset sales and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairments, major program restructuring activities,
constant currency and related adjustments, major program financing and hedging activities and other major items affecting comparability of operating results. See below for a description of adjustments to the company&#146;s U.S. GAAP financial
measures included herein. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-GAAP</FONT> information should be considered as supplemental in nature and is not meant to
be considered in isolation or as a substitute for the related financial information prepared in accordance with U.S. GAAP. In addition, the company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures may not be the same as or
comparable to similar <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> measures presented by other companies. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Because GAAP financial measures on a
forward-looking basis are not accessible and reconciling information is not available without unreasonable effort, the company has not provided that information with regard to the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures
in the company&#146;s outlook. Refer to the Outlook section below for more details. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>DEFINITIONS OF THE COMPANY&#146;S
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">NON-GAAP</FONT> FINANCIAL MEASURES </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company&#146;s <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial
measures and corresponding metrics reflect how the company evaluates its operating results currently and provide improved comparability of operating results. As new events or circumstances arise, these definitions could change. When these
definitions change, the company provides the updated definitions and presents the related <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> historical results on a comparable basis. When items no longer impact the company&#146;s current or future
presentation of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> operating results, the company removes these items from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> definitions. During 2018, the company added to the <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> definitions the exclusion of the impact from pension participation changes and remeasurement gains or losses related to remeasuring net monetary assets or liabilities in Argentina. </P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Organic Net Revenue&#148;</B> is defined as net revenues excluding the impacts of acquisitions;
divestitures; and currency rate fluctuations. The company also evaluates Organic Net Revenue growth from emerging markets and its Power Brands. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Adjusted Gross Profit&#148;</B> is defined as gross profit excluding the Simplify to Grow Program;
acquisition integration costs; the operating results of divestitures; <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivative contracts; and
incremental expenses related to the 2017 malware incident. The company also presents &#147;Adjusted Gross Profit margin,&#148; which is subject to the same adjustments as Adjusted Gross Profit. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s
Adjusted Gross Profit on a constant currency basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left" STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt"><B>&#147;Adjusted Operating Income&#148;</B> and <B>&#147;Adjusted Segment Operating Income&#148;</B> are defined
as operating income (or segment operating income) excluding the impacts of the items listed in the Adjusted Gross Profit definition as well as gains or losses (including <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> impairment charges) on
goodwill and intangible assets; divestiture or acquisition gains or losses and related divestiture, acquisition and integration costs; remeasurement of net monetary position; impacts from resolution of tax matters; CEO transition remuneration; and
impact from pension participation changes. The company also presents &#147;Adjusted Operating Income margin&#148; and &#147;Adjusted Segment Operating Income margin&#148;, which are subject to the same adjustments as Adjusted Operating Income and
Adjusted Segment Operating Income. The company also evaluates growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted Operating Income and Adjusted Segment Operating Income on a constant currency basis. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>

continuing operations excluding the impacts of the items listed in the Adjusted Operating Income definition as well as losses on debt extinguishment and related expenses; gain on equity method investment transactions; net earnings from divestitures;
gains or losses on interest rate swaps no longer designated as accounting cash flow hedges due to changed financing and hedging plans; and U.S. tax reform discrete impacts. Similarly, within Adjusted EPS, the company&#146;s equity method investment

expenditures. Free Cash Flow is the company&#146;s primary measure used to monitor its cash flow performance. </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">See the attached

<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>SEGMENT OPERATING INCOME </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company uses segment
operating income to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. The company believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze segment performance and trends. Segment operating income excludes unrealized gains and
losses on hedging activities (which are a component of cost of sales), general corporate expenses (which are a component of selling, general and administrative expenses), amortization of intangibles, gains and losses on divestitures and
acquisition-related costs (which are a component of selling, general and administrative expenses) in all periods presented. The company excludes these items from segment operating income in order to provide better transparency of its segment
operating results. Furthermore, the company centrally manages benefit plan <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-service</FONT> income and interest and other expense, net. Accordingly, the company does not present these items by segment because they
are excluded from the segment profitability measure that management reviews. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>ITEMS IMPACTING COMPARABILITY OF OPERATING RESULTS </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The following information is provided to give qualitative and quantitative information related to items impacting comparability of operating results. The
company identifies these based on how management views the company&#146;s business; makes financial, operating and planning decisions; and evaluates the company&#146;s ongoing performance. In addition, the company discloses the impact of changes in
currency exchange rates on the company&#146;s financial results in order to reflect results on a constant currency basis. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Divestitures,
Divestiture-related costs and Gains/(losses) on divestitures </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Divestitures include completed sales of businesses and exits of major product lines
upon completion of a sale or licensing agreement. Divestiture-related activity in 2018 and 2017 included: </P> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

</P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Acquisitions and Acquisition-related costs </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On June&nbsp;7, 2018, the company acquired a U.S. premium biscuit company, Tate&#146;s Bake Shop, within its North America segment and extended its premium
biscuit offerings. On a constant currency basis, the purchase added incremental net revenues of $22&nbsp;million in the three months and $52&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2018. In addition, the company incurred acquisition-related
costs of $13&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2018. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On November&nbsp;2, 2016, the company purchased from Burton&#146;s Biscuit Company
certain intangibles, which included the license to manufacture, market and sell Cadbury-branded biscuits in additional key markets around the world, including in the United Kingdom, France, Ireland, North America and Saudi Arabia. On a constant
currency basis, the purchase added incremental net revenues of $9&nbsp;million in the three months and $59&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2017. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Acquisition integration costs </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Within the
company&#146;s AMEA segment, in connection with the acquisition of a biscuit operation in Vietnam in 2015, the company recorded integration costs of $4&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2018 and $1&nbsp;million in the three months
ended and $3&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2017. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Simplify to Grow Program </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On September&nbsp;6, 2018, the company&#146;s Board of Directors approved an extension of the restructuring program through 2022, an increase of
$1.3&nbsp;billion in the program charges and an increase of $700&nbsp;million in capital expenditures. The current restructuring program, as increased and extended by these actions, is now called the Simplify to Grow Program. The primary objective
of the Simplify to Grow Program is to reduce the company&#146;s operating cost structure in both its supply chain and overhead costs. The program is intended primarily to cover severance as well as asset disposals and other manufacturing-related <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-time</FONT> costs. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Restructuring costs </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company recorded restructuring charges of $96&nbsp;million in the three months and $316&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2018 and
$117&nbsp;million in the three months and $535&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2017 within asset impairment and exit costs or benefit plan <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-service</FONT> income. These charges were for <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> asset write-downs (including accelerated depreciation and asset impairments), severance and other related costs. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Implementation costs </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Implementation costs primarily
relate to reorganizing the company&#146;s operations and facilities in connection with its supply chain reinvention program and other identified productivity and cost saving initiatives. The costs include incremental expenses related to the closure
of facilities, costs to terminate certain contracts and the simplification of the company&#146;s information systems. The company recorded implementation costs of $100&nbsp;million in the three months and $315&nbsp;million in the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2018 and $78&nbsp;million in the three months and $257&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2017. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Gain on equity method investment transactions </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On July&nbsp;9, 2018, Keurig Green Mountain, Inc. (&#147;Keurig&#148;) closed on its definitive merger agreement with Dr Pepper Snapple Group, Inc., and formed
Keurig Dr Pepper Inc. (&#147;KDP&#148;), a publicly traded company. Following the close of the transaction, the company&#146;s 24.2% investment in Keurig together with the company&#146;s shareholder loan receivable became a 13.8% investment in KDP.
During the third quarter of 2018, the company recorded a preliminary <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $757&nbsp;million reported as a gain on equity method transaction and $184&nbsp;million of deferred tax expense reported in
the provision for income taxes (or $573&nbsp;million <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">after-tax)</FONT> related to the change in the company&#146;s ownership interest while KDP finalizes the valuation for the transaction. During the company&#146;s
fourth quarter of 2018, KDP finalized its opening balance sheet and the company increased its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain by $21&nbsp;million to $778&nbsp;million for 2018. As the company continues to have significant
influence, the company continues to account for its investment in KDP under the equity method, resulting in recognizing its share of KDP earnings within the company&#146;s earnings and its share of KDP dividends within the company&#146;s cash flows.
In connection with this transaction, the company changed its accounting principle to reflect its share of Keurig&#146;s historical and KDP&#146;s ongoing earnings on a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-quarter</FONT> lag basis while the company
continues to record dividends when cash is received. The company determined a lag was preferable as it enables the company to continue to report its quarterly and annual results on a timely basis and to record its share of KDP&#146;s ongoing results
once KDP has publicly reported its results. This change in accounting principle was applied retrospectively to all periods. While the company&#146;s operating income did not change, equity method investment net earnings, net earnings and earnings
per share have been adjusted to reflect the lag across all reported periods. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On October&nbsp;2, 2017, the company completed the sale of one of its equity
method investments and recorded a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $40&nbsp;million within the gain on equity method investment transactions and $15&nbsp;million of tax expense. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Equity method investee adjustments </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Within
Adjusted EPS, the company&#146;s equity method investment net earnings exclude its proportionate share of its investees&#146; unusual or infrequent items, such as acquisition and divestiture-related costs and restructuring program costs. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and currency derivative contracts
</I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company excludes unrealized gains and losses <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(mark-to-market</FONT></FONT>
impacts) from outstanding commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> earnings measures until such time that the related exposures impact its operating results. The company
recorded net unrealized losses on commodity and forecasted currency transaction derivatives of $38&nbsp;million in the three months and net unrealized gains of $142&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2018 and net unrealized losses of
$27&nbsp;million in the three months and $96&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2017. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Intangible asset impairment charges
</I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the company&#146;s 2018 annual testing of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-amortizable</FONT> intangible assets, the company recorded
$68&nbsp;million of impairment charges in the third quarter of 2018 related to five trademarks. The impairments arose due to lower than expected product growth. The company recorded charges related to gum, chocolate, biscuits and candy trademarks of
$45&nbsp;million in Europe, $14&nbsp;million in North America and $9&nbsp;million in AMEA. The impairment charges were recorded within asset impairment and exit costs. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the company&#146;s 2017 annual testing of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-amortizable</FONT> intangible assets, the company recorded
$70&nbsp;million of impairment charges in the third quarter of 2017 related to five trademarks. The impairments arose due to lower than expected growth in part driven by decisions to redirect support from these trademarks to other regional and
global brands. The company recorded charges related to candy and gum trademarks of $52&nbsp;million in AMEA, $11&nbsp;million in Europe, $5&nbsp;million in Latin America and $2&nbsp;million in North America. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In addition, during the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2017, the company recorded a $38&nbsp;million intangible
asset impairment charge resulting from a category decline and lower than expected product growth related to a gum trademark in its North America segment as well as a $1&nbsp;million impairment related to a transaction. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Remeasurement of net monetary position </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the
second quarter of 2018, primarily based on published estimates which indicated that Argentina&#146;s three-year cumulative inflation rate exceeded 100%, the company concluded that Argentina became a highly inflationary economy for accounting
purposes. As of July&nbsp;1, 2018, the company began to apply highly inflationary accounting for its Argentinian subsidiaries and changed their functional currency from the Argentinian peso to the U.S. dollar. On July&nbsp;1, 2018, both monetary and
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-monetary</FONT> assets and liabilities denominated in Argentinian pesos were remeasured into U.S. dollars. As of each subsequent balance sheet date, Argentinian peso denominated monetary assets and liabilities
were remeasured into U.S. dollars using the exchange rate as of the balance sheet date, with remeasurement and other transaction gains and losses recorded in net earnings. The company recorded, related to the revaluation of the Argentinian peso
denominated net monetary assets, a remeasurement gain of $2&nbsp;million during the three months and a remeasurement loss of $11&nbsp;million during the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2018. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Incremental expenses related to the malware incident </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On June&nbsp;27, 2017, a global malware incident impacted the company&#146;s business. The malware affected a significant portion of the company&#146;s global
sales, distribution and financial networks. In the last four days of the second quarter and during the third quarter of 2017, the company executed business continuity and contingency plans to contain the impact, minimize damages and restore its
systems environment. To date, the company has not found, nor does the company expect to find, any instances of Company or personal data released externally. The company has also restored its main operating systems and processes and enhanced its
system security. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the second quarter of 2017, the company estimated that the malware incident had a negative impact of 2.3% on its net revenue growth
and 2.4% on its Organic Net Revenue growth. The company also incurred incremental expenses of $7&nbsp;million as a result of the incident. The company recognized the majority of delayed second quarter shipments in its third quarter 2017 results,
although the company permanently lost some revenue. On a 2017 full-year basis, the company estimated the loss of revenue had a negative impact of 0.4% on its net revenue and Organic Net Revenue growth. The company also incurred total incremental
expenses of $84&nbsp;million predominantly during the second half of 2017 as part of the recovery effort. The recovery from the incident was largely resolved by December&nbsp;31, 2017 and the company continued efforts to strengthen its security
measures and enhance general information technology, business process and disclosure controls. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Gain related to interest rate swaps </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company recognized a net <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> gain of $10&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2018, within interest
and other expense, net related to certain forward-starting interest rate swaps for which the planned timing of the related forecasted debt was changed. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Loss on debt extinguishment </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On April&nbsp;17,
2018, the company completed a cash tender offer and retired $570&nbsp;million of the long-term U.S. dollar debt. The company recorded a loss on debt extinguishment of $140&nbsp;million within interest and other expense, net related to the amount the
company paid to retire the debt in excess of its carrying value and from recognizing unamortized discounts, deferred financing and other cash costs in earnings at the time of the debt extinguishment. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On April&nbsp;12, 2017, the company discharged $488&nbsp;million of its 6.500% U.S. dollar-denominated debt. The company paid $504&nbsp;million, representing
principal as well as past and future interest accruals from February 2017 through the August 2017 maturity date. The company recorded an $11&nbsp;million loss on debt extinguishment within interest expense. </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Impact from resolution of tax matters </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">A tax indemnification matter related to the company&#146;s 2007 acquisition of the <I>LU</I> biscuit business was closed during the quarter ended June&nbsp;30,
2018. The closure had no impact on net earnings, however, it did result in a $15&nbsp;million tax benefit that was fully offset by an $11&nbsp;million expense in selling, general and administrative expenses and a $4&nbsp;million expense in interest
and other expense, net. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the first quarter of 2017, the Brazilian Supreme Court (the &#147;Court&#148;) ruled against the Brazilian tax authorities
in a leading case related to the computation of certain indirect <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(non-income)</FONT> taxes. The Court ruled that the indirect tax base should not include a value-added tax known as &#147;ICMS&#148;. By removing the
ICMS from the tax base, the Court effectively eliminated a &#147;tax on a tax.&#148; In lower courts, the company&#146;s Brazilian subsidiaries filed lawsuits to recover amounts paid and to discontinue subsequent payments related to the &#147;tax on
a tax.&#148; The Brazilian subsidiaries received injunctions against making payments for the &#147;tax on a tax&#148; in 2008 and since that time until December 2016, the company had accrued for this portion of the tax each quarter in the event that
the tax was reaffirmed by the Brazilian courts. On September&nbsp;30, 2017, based on legal advice and the publication of the Court&#146;s decision related to this case, the company determined that the likelihood that the increased tax base would be
reinstated and assessed against the company was remote. Accordingly, the company reversed its accrual of 667&nbsp;million Brazilian reais, or $212&nbsp;million as of September&nbsp;30, 2017, of which, $153&nbsp;million was recorded within selling,
general and administrative expenses and $59&nbsp;million was recorded within interest and other expense, net. In connection with the Court&#146;s 2017 decision, the Brazilian tax authority filed a motion seeking clarification and adjustment of the
terms of enforcement and that motion is still to be decided.&nbsp;The company continues to monitor developments in this matter and currently does not expect a material future impact on its financial statements. During the fourth quarter of 2018, in
one of the lower court cases, the Brazilian Federal Court of Appeals ruled in the company&#146;s favor against the Brazilian tax authority, allowing one of the company&#146;s Brazil subsidiaries to recover amounts previously paid. As a result, the
company recorded a net benefit in selling, general and administrative expenses of $26&nbsp;million. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">During the first quarter of 2017, the Spanish Supreme
Court decided, in the company&#146;s favor, an ongoing transfer pricing case with the Spanish tax authorities related to businesses Cadbury divested prior to the company&#146;s acquisition of Cadbury. As a result of the final ruling, during the
first quarter of 2017, the company recorded a favorable earnings impact of $46&nbsp;million in selling, general and administrative expenses and $12&nbsp;million in interest and other expense, net, for a total
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> impact of $58&nbsp;million due to the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> reversal of Cadbury-related accrued liabilities related to this matter. The company recorded a total of
$4&nbsp;million of income over the third and fourth quarters of 2017 in connection with the related bank guarantee releases. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>CEO transition
remuneration </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On November&nbsp;20, 2017, Dirk Van de Put succeeded Irene Rosenfeld as CEO of Mondel&#275;z International. In order to incent
Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put to join the company, the company provided him compensation to make him whole for incentive awards he forfeited or grants that were not made to him when he left his former employer. In connection with Irene Rosenfeld&#146;s
retirement, the company made her outstanding grants of performance share units for the 2016-2018 and 2017-2019 performance cycles eligible for continued vesting and paid $0.5&nbsp;million salary for her service as Chairman from January through March
2018. The company refers to these elements of Mr.&nbsp;Van de Put&#146;s and Ms.&nbsp;Rosenfeld&#146;s compensation arrangements together as &#147;CEO transition remuneration.&#148; </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company is excluding amounts it expenses as CEO transition remuneration from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> results because those
amounts are not part of the company&#146;s regular compensation program and are incremental to amounts the company would have incurred as ongoing CEO compensation. The company incurred CEO transition remuneration of $4&nbsp;million in the three
months and $22&nbsp;million in the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2018. During 2017, the company incurred CEO transition remuneration of $14&nbsp;million in the three months ended December&nbsp;31, 2017. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>U.S. tax reform discrete impacts </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">On
December&nbsp;22, 2017, the United States enacted tax reform legislation that included a broad range of business tax provisions, including but not limited to a reduction in the U.S. federal tax rate from 35% to 21% as well as provisions that limit
or eliminate various deductions or credits. The legislation also causes U.S. allocated expenses (e.g. interest and general </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
administrative expense) to be taxed and imposes a new tax on U.S. cross-border payments, Furthermore, the legislation includes a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-time</FONT> transition tax on
accumulated foreign earnings and profits. While clarifying guidance was issued by the IRS during 2018, further tax guidance is expected during 2019. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Certain impacts of the new legislation would have generally required accounting to be completed and incorporated into the company&#146;s 2017 <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">year-end</FONT> financial statements, however in response to the complexities of this new legislation, the SEC issued guidance to provide companies with relief. The SEC provided up to a
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">one-year</FONT> window for companies to finalize the accounting for the impacts of this new legislation. The company finalized its accounting for the new provisions during the fourth quarter of 2018. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The 2018 impact from finalizing the accounting for the new provisions was a discrete net tax expense of $19&nbsp;million, which is in addition to the
$44&nbsp;million discrete net tax benefit in the company&#146;s 2017 financial statements. The $19&nbsp;million expense in 2018 is primarily comprised of a $60&nbsp;million expense related to finalizing the changes in the company&#146;s indefinite
reinvestment assertion, partially offset by a $38&nbsp;million decrease to the transition tax estimated as of December&nbsp;31, 2017. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Impact from
pension participation changes </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The impact from pension participation changes represent the charges incurred when employee groups are withdrawn from
multiemployer pension plans and other changes in employee group pension plan participation. The company excludes these charges from its <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> results because those amounts do not reflect the company&#146;s
ongoing pension obligations. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In the fourth quarter of 2018, the company executed a complete withdrawal from the Bakery and Confectionery Union and
Industry International Pension Fund. The company estimated a withdrawal liability of $573&nbsp;million, which represents the company&#146;s best estimate of the withdrawal liability absent an assessment from the Fund. The company expects to pay the
liability over a period of 20 years from the date of the assessment. During 2018, within its North America segment, the company recorded a total discounted liability and related charge of $423&nbsp;million or $321&nbsp;million net of tax. The
company determined the net present value of the liability using a risk-free interest rate.&nbsp;The company recorded the <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-tax</FONT> <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> charges in selling, general and
administrative expense (and in other <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-cash</FONT> items, net in the consolidated statement of cash flows) and the liability in long-term other liabilities. During 2018, the company also recorded $6&nbsp;million of
accreted interest related to the long-term liability within interest and other expense, net. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Constant currency </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Management evaluates the operating performance of the company and its international subsidiaries on a constant currency basis. The company determines its
constant currency operating results by dividing or multiplying, as appropriate, the current period local currency operating results by the currency exchange rates used to translate the company&#146;s financial statements in the comparable prior-year
period to determine what the current period U.S. dollar operating results would have been if the currency exchange rate had not changed from the comparable prior-year period. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>OUTLOOK </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The company&#146;s outlook for 2019 Organic Net
Revenue growth, Adjusted EPS growth on a constant currency basis and Free Cash Flow are <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-GAAP</FONT> financial measures that exclude or otherwise adjust for items impacting comparability of financial results such
as the impact of changes in foreign currency exchange rates, restructuring activities, acquisitions and divestitures. The company is not able to reconcile its projected Organic Net Revenue growth to its projected reported net revenue growth for the
full-year 2019 because the company is unable to predict the impacts from potential acquisitions or divestitures as well as the impact of foreign exchange due to the unpredictability of future changes in foreign exchange rates, which could be
material as a significant portion of the company&#146;s operations are outside the U.S. The company is not able to reconcile its projected Adjusted EPS growth on a constant currency basis to its projected reported diluted EPS growth for the
full-year 2019 because the company is unable to predict the timing of its restructuring program costs, <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">mark-to-market</FONT></FONT> impacts from commodity and forecasted currency
transaction derivative contracts and impacts from potential acquisitions or divestitures as well as the impact of foreign exchange due to the unpredictability of future changes in foreign exchange rates, which could be material as a significant
portion of the company&#146;s operations are outside the U.S. The company is not able to reconcile its projected Free </P>

<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
Cash Flow to its projected net cash from operating activities for the full-year 2019 because the company is unable to predict the timing and amount of capital expenditures impacting cash flow.
Therefore, because of the uncertainty and variability of the nature and amount of future adjustments, which could be significant, the company is unable to provide a reconciliation of these measures without unreasonable effort. </P>
